ABSTRACT

TYPIC-ANSPEL/Operational
MANUAL
AMSPELL, Progress Report, January through June 1966
ACTION REQUIRED: FYI
REFERENCES: A. UFGT 16628
B. UFGT 15216
A. OPERATIONAL
1. During the period under review, financial support to the
PELL organization has been reduced significantly. As reported
in
proferences, the primary reason for the reduction was the
domesticities of many AMSPELL activities with current WOFACT
2100000
Operation between AMSPELL and the Station has been maintained
through AMHINT-2, the principal agent of the AMSPELL operation.
Although no longer being carried on a salted basis, AMHINT-2 has
continued to be responsive to Station guidance.
3. AMSPELL has continued its correspondence with various student
groups and leaders throughout the free world, and especially in
Latin America. AMSPELL has contacted various international student
groups requesting passage money so that its delegates could be
afforded the opportunity to attend upcoming international student
conference.
Based on:
1. The campaign was launched to call attention to the plight of
Pedro Luis BOITEL, a Cuban student lender who was unjustly
imprisoned on the Isle of Pines by the CASTRO regime. A report/
denunciation of the imprisonment of BOITEL was prepared and sent
to AMSPELL's principal contacts in the Latin American student field
seeking support for AMSPELL's demand that BOITEL be released.
(continued)

B. PRODUCTION
1. AMSPELL bi-monthly magazine (copy being forwarded under
separate cover)
a. AMSPELL efforts during recent months have been mainly
concentrated on the preparation of its new bi-monthly magazine.
8,000 copies of the magazine's first edition which was published
in May 1966 were distributed he follows:
(1) 3,000 copies sent to Latin America
(2) 1,000 copies distributed by AMSPELL delegations
(3) 1,000 copies distributed among Cubans in the United
States
(4)
100 copies were sent to AMSPELL contacts and
student movements in Europe, Africa, Asian, Canada, etc.
(5)
Members of the AMSPELL organization also received
a
1,000 copies of the American college bulletin was
inserted. Each member was asked to be a member of the
of subscriptions and advertising space as well as to
seek persons who would collaborate with the magazine
and their distribution, including their talents,
(6) The remainder of the American college in the various
embassies, official representations of governments and
organizations, both in the United States and abroad, as
well as among Cuban exile journalists and organizations
2. AMSPELL Cuban mailing
Since March 1966, 1,000 envelopes containing AMSPELL propa-
ganda have been mailed to Cuba on a monthly basis. This propaganda
is directed particularly at students who support the regime (copies
of the propaganda are being forwarded under separate cover).
3. Press
The majority of AMSPELL press releases have been in connection
with the statement of political prisoners by the Castro regime,
Other releases concerned the aforementioned BOITEL campaign and a
tribute to Cuban martyrs who gave their lives fighting against the
BATISTA dictatorship in 1957. (Copies of the press relenses are being
forwarded under separate cover.)
CINFINANCIAL
1. Final payment of AMSPELL salaries and termination bonusvas was
made in February in line with the Station's reduction of financial
support to AMSPELL. Under the present agreement JUNAVE support is
limited to $1,600 monthly, this includes the 2000 monthly financial
support payment to AMHINT-1's family, office overhead, and support for
printing/distributing the bi-monthly publication.
2. The following amounts were expended by the Station in support
of AMSPELL activities during the second half of FY 66:
Operational expenses
$ 9,929.74
Salaries and termination bonuses
6,200.00
Total expenditures
$16,129.74
D. FUTURE PLANS
It is anticipated that AMSPELL efforts in the near future will be
directed at the upcoming CLAE meeting which is scheduled to be held
in Havana 29 July to 9 August 1966.

SUBJECT
TYPIC/AMSPELL/Operational
ANSPELL Progress Report, November and December 1965
ACTION REQUIRED: FYI
REFERENCE: UFGA 23946, 24 November 1965
A. OPERATIONAL
1. General
During the period under review ANSPELL continued operations
aimed at the student/youth target. ANSPELL sent a circular letter
to students and youth in Cuba in an effort to establish a "dialogue"
between these young people and ANSPELL. Other ANSPELL activities
during this period are contained below.
2. Printed Propaganda.
a. Monthly ANSPELL Bulletin:
November
December
To Cuba
4,800
4,800
To Latin America (Spanish)
2,900
2,900
To Latin America (French)
1,925
1,925
To Latin America (English)
1,925
1,925
b. The regular bulletin highlighted the following themes:
The need for solidarity in the struggle for liberty for Cuban
political prisoners; the new trend in Polish communism and its
criticism toward the system; the attitude of Soviet students toward
tobacco industry. The failure of Castro's plan to indoctrinate
Cuban students. The December bulletin carried a special Christmas
message. (Copies of the problem are being sent for Headquarters
information under separate covers).

November and December without interruption. Topics discussed on
the program included: The war in Miet Nam; commenitaries supporting
work of studcet groups throughout the world in combating communism;
news of student and youth:activities in Cuth and Latin America;
world news reports; and a special Christmas message in December.
Press Releases
During the period under review, ANSPELL press releases,
themes of which are listed below, received replay as follows:
Dinrio las Americas; a. Tighter control ovor university
councils in Cuba.
b. Activities of Cuban agents in Mexico.
c. The large number of relatives of
high Cuban officials reported among refugees.
Bohemia Libre:
a. Reports on the exodus.
b. Comments on Cho Guevara's
disappearance and his wife's condition.
AMHIN:
a. ANSPELL comments on a Miami Herald
article concerning statements by Cuban students regarding the
incompatibility between Christianity and Communism.
b. Cuban agents reportedly responsible
for demonstrations against Secretary of State Denn Rusk and Senator
Robert Kennedy while on tours in Latin Amcinc.
c. Analysis of anti-Christian policies
in Cuban universities.

CONTINUATION OF
DISPATCH
SECRET
UFGA-23946
3. Radio Propaganda
AMSPELL continued its weekly radio programs and in addition
prepared tapes for distribution to numerous Latin American radio
stations. One such-tipe featured statements made by Alberto MILLER
before his imprisonment. Local Spanieh language stations also used
AMSPELL tapes.
Other developments
14
In September, AMBARB/54 and two other members of AMSPELL
resigned to seek other employment. The Station would appreciate current
information regarding KULAMP's interest and possible employment of
AMBARB/54 (per DIR 40/114). He is an intelligent and capable individual
and is currently investigating Job possibilities in ZRIETAL with
several international agencies.

C. FUTURE PLANS
AMSPELL will continue its political action and propaganda activities
during the coming months and will engage in special campaigns and press
releases as current developments dictate.

DISPATCH
To
Chief, WH
INDU
COS, Caracas
FROM
Chief of Station, JNWAVE
SUBJECT
D'YUOR/PBRUNEN/AMSPELL/Operational
C AMHINT-2 Trip to Caracas
ACTION HOURS
AR:
1. Subject, Identity A, recently visited Caracas for the purpose
of obtaining his residence visa and while there was in contact with
the local ANSPELL delegation as well as with representatives of the
major student political groups at the Central University in Caracas
(UCV). AMHINT-2 was particularly interested in promoting a productive
working relationship between ANSPELL in Caracas and Identity B, which
appears to be a new Christian-oriented group organized to provide Liceo
students with courses and seminars in fighting communis. A copy of
the Identity B, which is a member of the Board of Directors.
On his return, AMHINT-2 reported on the present composition
of the local ANSPELL group. He indicated that Identity C, who first
joined ANSPELL in 1960 in Cuba and who recently arrived in Venezuela
from Santo Domingo, has replaced Identity D as leader of the group.
A list containing the names of the other members of the delegation,
as well as a brief description of their ANSPELL duties, is also
forwarded under separate cover, Attachment No. 2.
3. At present, the ANSPELL group in Caracas is concentrating its
efforts on working with Identity B and in maintaining good relations
with the press in order to carry out propaganda at the past cost with
such groups as the Josee Marti Patriotic Club and the UCE.
4. The ANSPELL delegation is in contact with a number of student
political leaders not only at UCV but at several of the other universi-
ties. These contacts include Identities E, F, G, H and I.
A
Athatments:
1. Brochure, u/sec
2. Description of Duties, u/sc
3. Identities, u/sc
DISTRIBUTION:
3-WH, w/3 attachments
2-MH/CW/attachment Nos 1&3

SUBJECT
TYPIC/AMSPELL/Operational
ANSPELL Progress Report - March 1965
CTOKING REPORT: STURKERS
FYI
REF: A. UFGA 20,729, 26 March 1965
B. UFGA 20,262, 9 March 1965
A. OPERATIONAL ACTIVITIES
1. General
ANSPELL has continued its normal propaganda activities
as outlined below. On 23 March 1965, AMBITT-2 agreed to the terms
outlined in Reference B, including a substantial budget reduction,
to become effective 1 April. ANSPELL's chief problem at the present
time is to liquidate debts incurred as a result of the defunct
ANSPELL paramilitary operation.
2. Propaganda
a. The March 1965 edition of the regular AMSPELL newspaper
was mailed to Latin America and AMSPELL delegations in the U. S.
(9,800 copies), attachment No. 1 under separate cover.
b. The March 1965 edition of the pony AMSPELL newspaper was
mailed into Cuba (4,800 copies), attachment No. 2 under separate
cover.
c. The AMSPELL international bulletin was mailed to its
normal recipients during March 1965. Spanish edition -- 2,900
copies, attachment No. 3. French edition -- 1,925 copies, attachment
No. 4. English edition -- 1,925 copies, attachment No. 5.
/ CONTINUED /

CLASSIFICATION
TOPIATCH SYMBOL AND NUVSE
CONTINUATION OF
DISPATCH
S E C R E T
d. In connection with the prisoners' campaign (paragraph
5(a) below), 10,000 copies of the Prisoners' Message were printed,
attachment No. 6; 5,000 copies of a letter to Chilcan President
Eduardo Frei, attachment No. 7; 5,000 circular letters to Latin
Amorican Identity A organizations; attachment No. 8; and 5,000
copies of a circular letter to ANSPELL Delogates, attachment No. 9.
3. Radio Propaganda
ANSPELL continued its regular radio operations consisting of
a 15-minute program Tuesdays through Saturdays on ATHIGH, and a
15-minute program broadcast every Monday over WINE and several Latin
American stations.
4. Press Releases
Miscellaneous press releases are included as attachment No. 10,
under separate cover.
5. Other Activities.
a. The prisoners' campaign got off to a slow start. The
Identity B meeting in March, which was supposed to have been the
kick-off of the campaign, did not produce the expected results.
The American Indian American tour and was unable to attend,
and Identity D, who had promised to push the prisoners' cause at the
meeting, limited himself to pleas for Cuban Identity E prisoners.
The letter written to Chillean Prosident Eduardo Frei (attachment No. 7)
was signed by the American Indian American Society for the American
the AN SPELL delegation in Santiago for olivory to the President. The
Chilean
collections,
followed
by
the
earthquake
complicated
this
plan
and the delivery of the letter was delayed. (See paragraph 2-d above
for information re propaganda printed by AN SPELL in connection with
the campaign).
b. In connection with the 13 March anniversary of the
assault of the American Industrial Palace, AN SPELL issued a press
release on the Cuban Press, 10), all publications contained appropriate
editorials and, in addition to full coverage on the regular AN SPELL
radio programs, additional radio coverage was obtained on JMHOPE
and AMTIIGH with a social interview. The AN SPELL publication re
the anniversary is attached under separate cover, No. 11.
c. The AN SPELL delegation in Mexico participated in the
tribute to Venezuelan workers (CTV) organized by the Cubans residing
in Mexico City. (See attachment No. 10 for pertinent press reiones.)
Activities of other AN SPELL Delegations including publications and
press releases are included under attachment No. 12.

DISPATCH

Deputy Chief, WH/SA
INFO
FROM
Chief of Station, JAWAVE
SUBJECT.
TYPIC/ANSPELL/Operational
C. AMSPELL Progress Report -- January and February 1965
ACTION GROUPS: STRATEGIES
FYI:
REF: UFGA 19,393, 18 January 1965
A. OPERATIONAL ACTIVITIES:
1. General.
ANSPELL operational activities during January and February
were of a routine nature, details of which are noted in the paragraphs
below. AMSPELL-KUBARK relations have continued to deteriorate since
the collapse of the AMSPELL paramilitary effort in the fall of 1964, and
at the end of February the Station decided to reduce the AMSPELL sub-
sidy. This problem was discussed in UFGA. 20,262, 9 March 1965. We
shall start implementing this decision at the beginning of April.
2. Propaganda.
a. The January and February 1965 editions of the regular
AMSFELL newspaper were mailed to Latin America and AMSPELL delegations
in the U. S. (9,800 copies each), attachment No. 1 under separate
cover. This represents a planned reduction from the previous 19,800
monthly figure.
b. The January and February 1965 editions of the pony ANSPELL
newspaper were mailed into Cuba (4,800 copies each), attachment No. 2
under separate cover.
c. The AMSPELL international bulletin was mailed to its
normal recipients during January and February 1965. Spanish editions-
2,900 copies each, attachment No. 3. French edition--1,925 copies
each, attachment No. 4. English edition--1,925 copies each, attach-
ment No. 5.
CONTINUED /

d. 5,000 copies of the leaflet enclosed ns attachment No. 6
were mailed to Cubaduring January.
e. 10,000 copies of attachment No. 7 have been printed and
will be distributed in Latin America in connection with the prisoners
campaign discussed in paragraph C below.
3. Radio Propaganda.
AMSPELL continued its regular radio operations consisting of
a 15-minute program daily except Sunday on ANTHIGH, and a 15-minute
program broadcast every Monday over WMIIE and several Latin American
stations.
4. Other Activities.
CARA 9922 and related traffic discussed problems with AMSPELL
representatives in Garacas.

C. FUTURE PLANS:
AMSPELL is planning a publicity campaign in cooperation with Identity
to publicize the situation of prisoners in Cuba. The major phase of
this campaign will not be launched until the March executive-committee
meeting of Identity. AMSPELL requires in Santiago, Chile, who
are local station assets, will also launch a related campaign regarding
AMSPELL martyrs in prison (See WAVE 9497).

DISPATCH
TO
Deputy Chief, WH/SA
BPG
FROM
Chief of Station, JMWAVE AKB
BRUGGET TYPIC/AMSPELL/Operational
t AMSPELL Progress Report - December 1984
ACTION REQUIRED: PROTECUECE
FYI:
REF: UFGA 19,195, 28 December 1964
A. OPERATIONAL ACTIVITIES
1. General.
AMSPELL has so far survived the internal crisis brought about
by the collapse of its military activity noted in the previous progress
report. However, AMSPELL is still faced with a severe financial
problem resulting from the termination of the military activity.
AMHINT-2 states that AMSPELL has $12,000.00 in the 19th century which
has been a major challenge to the crisis. The finding paid off at the
rate of $1,300.00 per month. AMHINT-2 is trying to sell the AMSPELL
boats in order to liquidate these debts. So far he has had little
success. AMHINT-2 has said that he does not intend to give up the
reduction of the military and the military. The most important
will not conduct new military operations in the future without ODYOKE
assistance and concurrence. According to AMHINT-2 lack of funds and
intelligence information together with pressure by ODYOKE on Dominican
authorities frustrated the AMSPELL military operation, and he has no
intention of going through a similar disastrous experience again.
2. Propaganda.
a. 19,800 copies of the regular AMSPELL newspaper were mailed
to Latin America and AMSPELL delegations in the United States. (Attach-
ment No. 1, under separate cover.)
Attachments:
1 thru 6, As stated, u/sec
Distribution:
3
DC/WH/SA, w/attacks, u/sc
CASSIFICATION
SECRET
CLASSIFICATION

/ CONTINUED /

SUBJECT
DIFACTICR BYMOUL AND NUMBER
S E C R E T
UFGA 19,393
DISPATCH
DISPATCH
b. 4,800 copies of the pony AMSPELL newspaper wore mailed
into Cuban (Attachment No. 2, under separate cover.) Both the pony
and regular editions stress the conflict between the old-guard and the
"new-guard" communists; the boycott declared by the Venezuelan trade
unions, the confession of failure made by Castro in his speech at the
University of Havana, and an analysis of the situation at the Cuban
universities before and after Castro.
c. 2,900 copies of the December issue of the Spanish language
edition of the AMSPELL bulletin were mailed to Latin American recipients
(Attachment No. 3, under separate cover.) Of particular interest is
the article on page 2 which discusses the recent Congo atrocities.
d. 1,925 copies each of the November issue of the French and
English editions of the AMSPELL bulletin were mailed to overseas areas.
(Attachment No. 4, under separate cover.)
3. Radio Propaganda.
AMPEL! continued its regular radio operations consisting of
a 10-minute program daily except Sunday on ANTHIGH, and a 10-minute
program broadcast every Monday over WME and several Latin America
stations. Representative themes were: Congo atrocities inspired by
Communists, Venezuelan student support of the Cuban cause; Argent
the American American Association of the American American crisis
in Cuba; factional struggle of the Cuban regime; desperate measures
undertakon by the regime to prevent a disaster in the sugar industry;
statement of a Venezuelan student regarding the training in Cuba of
1,500 Latin American youth in terrorist activities; more on the
Congolese situation; transportation in Castro's Cuba; factional
struggle in the Cuban regime; Che Quevara's speech in the United
Nations creates tense situation between Cuba and the USSH; and Bala
Roca working for thedomrial of Castro.
4. Press Releases.
Miscellaneous press releases are included as Attachment No. 5
under separate cover.
5. Other Activities.
a. WAVE 5843 dated 8 December 1964 forwarded a candidate for
an AMSPELL position in the Dominican Republic.
b. AMSPELL requested that AMBARD-58 be sent to Ecuador to
replace AMBARD-28 who was resigning. (WAVE 5842 dated 8 December 1964)
The Quito station was listed that AMBARD-28 functions had been taken over
by ECPLY-2, and the AMBARD-58's services were not required (QUIT 6805
dated 11 October 1964).
c. Attachment No. 6 is a copy of an English-language bulletin
produced by AMSPELL without direct KUBARK support which is sent to
recipients in the U. S. Pressure will be brought to bear on AMHINT-2
to drop this publication entirely on the grounds that it is not the
purpose of AMSPELL to propagandize U. S. citizens.

CONTINUATION OF
S E C R E T
UFGA 21,738
C. A document on political prisoners in Cuba was mailed to
Latin American and other international addresses. The Spanish version
was mailed in 10,000 copies and the English version in 5,000 copies
(Attachment Nos. 5 and 6). An open letter to the President of Chile
on the subject of political prisoners was disseminated in 5,000 copies
(Attachment No. 7. under separate cover.) Press releases and news
clips on the prisoners campaign are enclosed. (Attachment No. 8,
under separate cover.)
d. Miscellaneous Press Releases and Clippings are enclosed.
(Attachment No. 9, under separate cover.)
3. Radio Propaganda.
Beginning 12 April AMSPELL radio operations were reduced to a
15-minute program Monday on AHTHIGH and a local station. This program
is also played on several Latin American stations.
4. Relations with Other Organizations.
AMSPELL received a number of letters from groups and individuals
interested in information on Cuba. Some of the groups who wrote to
AMSPELL were: Portuguese University Center, World Assembly of Youth,
International Union of Young Christian Democratic Workers
Confidential, 1999, 1999, 1999, 2000, and of Argentina, Christian
Social Democratic Party Youth of Colombia, International Institute of
Social Studies (CLASC), Mexican Newsmen Association, National Union
of Malaysian Students, and individual Mexican and Dominican Students.
(Copies of these letters are forwarded in Attachment No. 10, under
separate cover.)
B. FUNDS EXPENDED

$ 3,250.00

3,850.00

1,215.00
Extra mailing expense

C. FUTURE PLANS
An AMSPELL member was invited by the Paraguayan group to visit
them for May 20 celebrations.
AMSPELL was also invited by the International Student Association
of Japan to participate at an International Students Conference to
be held in Japan from July 22 to August 9, however, the station does
not intend to encourage AMSPELL participation.
Hume / / KELLEN
ANDREW K. REUTEMAN
